</tr>
</table>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_world_food_price_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>A May 2008 national survey found that food banks and pantries across the US were being forced to cut back on food distribution as 99 percent of respondents reported an increase in the number of people requesting services. Rising food and fuel prices, inadequate food stamp benefits, unemployment, underemployment, and rent or mortgage costs were factors reported as forcing an average of 15–20 percent more people.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> Compounding this issue, USDA bonus foods have declined by $200 million and local food donations were down nationally about 9 percent over the same period. According to the California Association of Food Banks, which is an umbrella organization of nearly all food banks in the state, food banks are at the "beginning of a crisis."<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Effects_on_farmers">Effects on farmers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_world_food_price_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Effects on farmers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>If global price movements are transmitted to local markets, <a href="/wiki/Farmer" title="Farmer">farmers</a> in the developing world could benefit from the rising price of food. According to researchers from the <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Development_Institute" title="Overseas Development Institute">Overseas Development Institute</a>, this may depend on farmers' capacity to respond to changing market conditions. Experience suggests that farmers lack the credit and inputs needed to respond in the short term. In the medium or long term, however, they could benefit, as seen in the Asian <a href="/wiki/Green_Revolution" title="Green Revolution">Green Revolution</a> or in many African countries in the recent past.<sup id="cite_ref-bpdnsw_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bpdnsw-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Relationship_with_2008_Chinese_milk_scandal">Relationship with 2008 Chinese milk scandal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_world_food_price_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Relationship with 2008 Chinese milk scandal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">For more details on this topic, see <a href="/wiki/2008_Chinese_milk_scandal" title="2008 Chinese milk scandal">2008 Chinese milk scandal</a>.</div>
<p>As grain prices increased, China's numerous small-holding milk farmers, as well as producers of feed for cattle, were unable to exist economically. As a result, they turned to putting additives into the feed and milk, including <a href="/wiki/Melamine" title="Melamine">melamine</a>, in order to boost the measured level of protein. Hundreds of thousands of children became ill, China's milk exports virtually ended, executives and officials were arrested and some executed, and companies went bankrupt.<sup id="cite_ref-tele1_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tele1-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Unrest_and_government_actions_in_individual_countries_and_regions">Unrest and government actions in individual countries and regions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_world_food_price_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Unrest and government actions in individual countries and regions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The price rises affected parts of <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Asia" title="Economy of Asia">Asia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Africa" title="Economy of Africa">Africa</a> particularly severely with <a href="/wiki/Burkina_Faso" title="Burkina Faso">Burkina Faso</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a>, Senegal, <a href="/wiki/Mauritania" title="Mauritania">Mauritania</a>, Côte d'Ivoire,<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> seeing protests and <a href="/wiki/List_of_riots" title="List of riots">riots</a> in late 2007 and early 2008 over the unavailability of basic food staples. Other countries that have seen food riots or are facing related unrest are: <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, Bolivia, <a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">Yemen</a>, Uzbekistan, <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> and South Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_world_food_price_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Bangladesh">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>10,000 workers rioted close to the Bangladeshi capital <a href="/wiki/Dhaka" title="Dhaka">Dhaka</a>, smashing cars and buses and vandalising factories in anger at high food prices and low wages. Dozens of people, including at least 20 police officials, were injured in the violence. Ironically, the country achieved food self-sufficiency in 2002, but food prices increased drastically due to the reliance of agriculture on oil and fossil fuels.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<p>Economists estimate 30 million of the country's 150 million people could go hungry.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Brazil">Brazil</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_world_food_price_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Brazil">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In April 2008, the Brazilian government announced a temporary ban on the export of rice. The ban is intended to protect domestic consumers.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Burkina_Faso">Burkina Faso</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_world_food_price_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Burkina Faso">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>One of the earlier food riots took place in <a href="/wiki/Burkina_Faso" title="Burkina Faso">Burkina Faso</a>, on 22 February, when rioting broke out in the country's second and third largest cities over soaring food prices (up to a 65 percent increase), sparing the capital, <a href="/wiki/Ouagadougou" title="Ouagadougou">Ouagadougou</a>, where soldiers were mobilized throughout strategic points. The government promised to lower taxes on food and to release food stocks. Over 100 people were arrested in one of the towns.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> Related policy actions of the Burkinabe government included:</p>
<ul>
<li>The removal of customs duty on rice, salt, dairy-based products and baby foods</li>
<li>The removal of value added tax on durum wheat, baby foods, soap and edible oils</li>
<li>Establishing negotiated prices with wholesalers for sugar, oil and rice</li>
<li>Releasing food stocks</li>
<li>Strengthening of community grain banks</li>
<li>Food distribution in-kind</li>
<li>Reduction of electricity cost, partial payment of utility bills for the poor</li>
<li>Enacting special programs for schools and hospitals</li>
<li>Fertilizer distribution and production support.</li>
</ul>
<p>A ban was also imposed on exportation of cereals.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cameroon">Cameroon</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_world_food_price_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Cameroon">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2008_Cameroonian_anti-government_protests" title="2008 Cameroonian anti-government protests">2008 Cameroonian anti-government protests</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a>, the world's fourth largest <a href="/wiki/Cocoa_bean" title="Cocoa bean">cocoa</a> producer, saw large scale rioting in late February 2008 in Douala, the country's commercial capital. Protesters were against inflating food and fuel prices, as well as the attempt by President <a href="/wiki/Paul_Biya" title="Paul Biya">Paul Biya</a> to extend his 25-year rule. Protesters set up barricades, burned tires, and targeted businesses that they believed belonged to the Biya family, high members of the ruling party, the government, or France.<sup id="cite_ref-Amin_2012_20.E2.80.9343_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Amin_2012_20.E2.80.9343-113">[113]</a></sup> It became the first protest in the nation's history in which minute- by-minute events were covered by social media. By 27 February, a strike was taking place in thirty-one cities, including Yaoundé, Douala, Bamenda, Bafoussam, Buea, Limbe, Tiko, Muea, Mutengene, and Kumba.<sup id="cite_ref-Amin_2012_20.E2.80.9343_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Amin_2012_20.E2.80.9343-113">[113]</a></sup> At least seven people were killed in the worst unrest seen in the country in over fifteen years.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> This figure was later increased to 24.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-95">[95]</a></sup> Youths were mobilized in ways that had not been seen since the days of the villes mortes.<sup id="cite_ref-Amin_2012_20.E2.80.9343_113-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Amin_2012_20.E2.80.9343-113">[113]</a></sup> Part of the government response to the protests was a reduction in import taxes on foods including rice, flour, and fish. The government reached an agreement with retailers by which prices would be lowered in exchange for the reduced import taxes. As of late April 2008, however, reports suggested that prices had not eased and in some cases had even increased.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 24 April 2008, the government of Cameroon announced a two-year emergency program designed to double Cameroon's food production and achieve food self-sufficiency.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="C.C3.B4te_d.27Ivoire">Côte d'Ivoire</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_world_food_price_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Côte d'Ivoire">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 31 March, <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B4te_d%27Ivoire" class="mw-redirect" title="Côte d'Ivoire">Côte d'Ivoire</a>'s capital <a href="/wiki/Abidjan" title="Abidjan">Abidjan</a> saw police use tear gas and a dozen protesters injured following food riots that gripped the city. The riots followed dramatic hikes in the price of food and fuel, with the price of beef rising from US$1.68 to $2.16 per kilogram, and the price of gasoline rising from $1.44 to $2.04 per liter, in only three days.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Egypt">Egypt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_world_food_price_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Egypt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, a boy was killed from a gunshot to the head after Egyptian police intervened in violent demonstrations over rising food prices that gripped the industrial city of <a href="/wiki/El-Mahalla_El-Kubra" class="mw-redirect" title="El-Mahalla El-Kubra">Mahalla</a> on 8 April. Large swathes of the population have been hit as food prices, and particularly the price of bread, have doubled over the last several months as a result of producers exploiting a shortage that has existed since 2006<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup>&#160;<b>·</b> .<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_world_food_price_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Ethiopia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg" class="image"><img alt="[icon]" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" width="20" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="31" /></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span"><b>This section needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_world_food_price_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small> <small><i>(June 2008)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Drought and the food price crisis threatened thousands in <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Haiti">Haiti</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_world_food_price_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Haiti">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 12 April 2008, the Haitian Senate voted to dismiss Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Jacques-%C3%89douard_Alexis" title="Jacques-Édouard Alexis">Jacques-Édouard Alexis</a> after violent food riots hit the country.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> The food riots caused the death of 5 people.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_95-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-95">[95]</a></sup> Prices for food items such as rice, beans, fruit and condensed milk have gone up 50 percent in <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a> since late 2007 while the price of fuel has tripled in only two months.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> Riots broke out in April due to the high prices, and the government had been attempting to restore order by subsidizing a 15 percent reduction in the price of rice.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> As of February 2010, post-earthquake Port-au-Prince is almost entirely reliant on foreign food aid, some of which ends up in the black markets.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="India">India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_world_food_price_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: India">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>India has banned the export of rice except for Basmati which attracts a premium price.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup></p>
<p>The ban has since been removed, and India now exports a variety of rice.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="reliable source needed for this claim (December 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Indonesia">Indonesia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_world_food_price_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Indonesia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Street protests over the price of food took place in <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> where food staples and gasoline have nearly doubled in price since January 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-gm-I_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gm-I-127">[127]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Latin_America">Latin America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_world_food_price_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Latin America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In April 2008, the Latin American members of the United Nations' <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Agriculture_Organization" title="Food and Agriculture Organization">Food and Agriculture Organization</a> (FAO) met in <a href="/wiki/Bras%C3%ADlia" title="Brasília">Brasília</a> to confront the issues of high food prices, scarcities and violence that affect the region.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mexico">Mexico</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_world_food_price_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Mexico">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Mexico" title="President of Mexico">President of Mexico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Felipe_Calder%C3%B3n" title="Felipe Calderón">Felipe Calderón</a>, with industry representatives and members of the Confederation of Industrial Chambers (Concamin), agreed to freeze prices of more than 150 consumer staples, such as coffee, sardines, tuna, oil, soup or tea, among others, until the end of December 2008. The measure was carried out in an attempt to control inflation, which stood at an annual rate of 4.95%, the highest increase since December 2004.</p>
<p>Mexican baking company <a href="/wiki/Grupo_Bimbo" title="Grupo Bimbo">Grupo Bimbo</a>'s CEO, Daniel Servitje, announced in the 19th Plenary Meeting of the Mexico–China Business Committee that Bimbo agreed to freeze their product prices, despite a 20% rise in production costs.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> Bimbo is one of the most important baking companies worldwide, having recently expanded to China. Bimbo has also acquired five bakeries in the United States and Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mozambique">Mozambique</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_world_food_price_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Mozambique">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In mid February, rioting that started in the Mozambican rural town of <a href="/wiki/Chokwe,_Mozambique" title="Chokwe, Mozambique">Chokwe</a> and then spread to the capital, <a href="/wiki/Maputo" title="Maputo">Maputo</a>, has resulted in at least four deaths. The riots were reported in the media to have been, at least in part, over food prices and were termed "food riots." A biofuel advocacy publication, however, claimed that these were, in fact, "fuel riots", limited to the rise in the cost of diesel, and argued that the "food riot" characterization worked to fan "anti-biofuels sentiment."<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pakistan">Pakistan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_world_food_price_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Pakistan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Pakistan_Army" title="Pakistan Army">Pakistan Army</a> has been deployed to avoid the seizure of food from fields and warehouses. This hasn't stopped the food prices from increasing. The new government has been blamed for not managing the countries food stockpiles properly.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Myanmar">Myanmar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_world_food_price_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Myanmar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Once the world's top rice producer, <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a> has produced enough rice to feed itself until now. Rice exports dropped over four decades from nearly 4 million tons to only about 40,000 tons last year, mostly due to neglect by Myanmar's ruling generals of infrastructure, including irrigation and warehousing. On 3 May 2008 <a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Nargis" title="Cyclone Nargis">Cyclone Nargis</a> stripped Myanmar's rice-growing districts, ruining large areas with salt water. U.N. Food and Agriculture Organization estimates that these areas produce 65 percent of Myanmar's rice. Worries of long-term food shortages and rationing are rife. The military regime says nothing about the rice crisis, but continues to export rice at the same rate. "...at least the next two harvests are going to be greatly affected and there'll be virtually no output from those areas during that time. So we're likely to see considerable food and rice shortages for the next couple of years. The damage to the economy is going to be profound." said economist and Myanmar expert Sean Turnell, of Australia's Macquarie University. (interviewed in "The Irriwaddy", Tuesday, 27 May 2008)</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Panama">Panama</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_world_food_price_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Panama">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Panama, in response to higher rice prices the government began buying rice at the high market price and selling rice to the public at a lower subsidized price at food kiosks.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philippines">Philippines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_world_food_price_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Philippines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Gloria_Macapagal-Arroyo" class="mw-redirect" title="Gloria Macapagal-Arroyo">Arroyo government</a> insisted on 13 April that there would be no food riots in the country and that there could be no comparison with Haiti's situation.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> Chief Presidential Legal Counsel, <a href="/wiki/Sergio_Apostol" title="Sergio Apostol">Sergio Apostol</a> stated that: "Haiti is not trying to solve the problem, while we are doing something to address the issue. We don't have a food shortage. So, no comparison..."<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> Comments by the Justice Secretary, <a href="/wiki/Raul_M._Gonzalez" title="Raul M. Gonzalez">Raul Gonzalez</a>, the following day, that food riots are not far fetched, were quickly rebuked by the rest of the government.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 15 April, the Philippines, the world's largest rice importer, urged China, Japan, and other key Asian nations, to convene an emergency meeting, especially taking issue with those countries' rice export bans. "Free trade should be flowing", Philippine Agriculture Secretary Arthur Yap stated.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> In late April 2008, the Philippines government requested that the World Bank exert pressure on rice exporting countries to end export restrictions.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Russia">Russia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_world_food_price_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Russia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Russian government pressured retailers to freeze food prices before key elections for fear of a public backlash against the rising cost of food in October 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> The freeze ended on 1 May 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Senegal">Senegal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_world_food_price_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Senegal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 31 March 2008, <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a> had riots in response to the rise in the price of food and fuel. Twenty-four people were arrested and detained in a response that one local human rights group claimed included "torture" and other "unspeakable acts" on the part of the security forces.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> Further protests took place in <a href="/wiki/Dakar" title="Dakar">Dakar</a> on 26 April 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Somalia">Somalia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_world_food_price_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Somalia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Riots in Somalia occurred on 5 May 2008 over the price of food, in which five protesters were killed. The protests occurred amid a serious humanitarian emergency due to the <a href="/wiki/War_in_Somalia_(2006%E2%80%932009)" class="mw-redirect" title="War in Somalia (2006–2009)">Ethiopian war in Somalia</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tajikistan">Tajikistan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_world_food_price_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Tajikistan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Christian_Science_Monitor" title="The Christian Science Monitor">The Christian Science Monitor</a></i>, neweurasia, and other media observers are predicting that a nascent hunger crisis will erupt into a full <a href="/wiki/Famine" title="Famine">famine</a> as a consequence of the <a href="/wiki/2008_Central_Asia_energy_crisis" title="2008 Central Asia energy crisis">energy shortages</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-neweurasia_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-neweurasia-142">[142]</a></sup> UN experts announced on 10 October that almost one-third of <a href="/wiki/Tajikistan" title="Tajikistan">Tajikistan</a>'s 6.7 million inhabitants may not have enough to eat for the winter of 2008–09.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Yemen">Yemen</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_world_food_price_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Yemen">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Food riots in southern <a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">Yemen</a> that began in late March and continued through early April, saw police stations torched, and roadblocks were set up by armed protesters. The army has deployed tanks and other military vehicles. Although the riots involved thousands of demonstrators over several days and over 100 arrests, officials claimed no fatalities; residents, however, claimed that at least one of the fourteen wounded people has died.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Projections">Projections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_world_food_price_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Projections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/FAO" class="mw-redirect" title="FAO">UN (FAO)</a> released a study in December 2007 projecting a 49 percent increase in African cereal prices, and 53 percent in European prices, through July 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> In April 2008, the World Bank, in combination with the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>, announced a series of measures aimed at mitigating the crisis, including increased loans to African farmers and emergency monetary aid to badly affected areas such as Haiti.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> According to FAO director <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Diouf" title="Jacques Diouf">Jacques Diouf</a>, however, the <a href="/wiki/World_Food_Programme" title="World Food Programme">World Food Programme</a> needs an immediate cash injection of at least $1700 million,<sup id="cite_ref-gm_11-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gm-11">[11]</a></sup> far more than the tens of million-worth in measures already pledged. On 28 April 2008, the United Nations Secretary-General <a href="/wiki/Ban_Ki-moon" title="Ban Ki-moon">Ban Ki-moon</a> established a Task Force on the Global Food Security Crisis <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.un.org/issues/food/taskforce/">[2]</a> under his chairmanship and composed of the heads of the United Nations specialized agencies, funds and programmes, Bretton Woods institutions and relevant parts of the UN Secretariat to co-ordinate efforts to alleviate the crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="After_the_crisis">After the crisis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_world_food_price_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: After the crisis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>2013 research concluded that the spike was the result of an unusual combination of circumstances and prices in the future will be higher than before the spike, depending on <a href="/wiki/Oil_prices" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil prices">oil prices</a>, <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>, and future diets. The impacts of the spike on poor people were concentrated in low-income countries and may have been less severe than once thought, thanks to rising rural wages in some countries. The researchers called on developing countries to ensure good data on the key indicators of distress and to strengthen <a href="/wiki/Social_protection" title="Social protection">social protection</a>, and on those involved in international development to continue increasing focus on reducing child <a href="/wiki/Malnutrition" title="Malnutrition">malnutrition</a> and stimulating agricultural development.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Actions_by_governments">Actions by governments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_world_food_price_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Actions by governments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/IFAD" class="mw-redirect" title="IFAD">IFAD</a> is making up to US$200 million available to support poor farmers boost food production in face of the global food crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 2 May 2008, US President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> said he was asking Congress to approve an extra $770 million funding for international food aid.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> On 16 October 2008, in a speech at a United Nations gathering on <a href="/wiki/World_Food_Day" title="World Food Day">World Food Day</a>, former US president <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a> criticized the bipartisan coalition in Congress that blocked efforts to make some aid donations in cash rather than in food.<sup id="cite_ref-sfgate.com_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sfgate.com-151">[151]</a></sup> Referring in part to policies that had pressured African governments to reduce subsidies for fertilizer and other agricultural inputs, Clinton also said:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>We need the World Bank, the IMF, all the big foundations, and all the governments to admit that, for 30 years, we all blew it, including me when I was President. We were wrong to believe that food was like some other product in international trade, and we all have to go back to a more responsible and sustainable form of agriculture.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>The release of Japan's rice reserves onto the market may bring the rice price down significantly. As of 16 May, anticipation of the move had already lowered prices by 14% in a single week.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 30 April 2008 Thailand announced the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_Rice_Exporting_Countries" class="mw-redirect" title="Organization of Rice Exporting Countries">Organization of Rice Exporting Countries</a> (OREC) with the potential to develop a price-fixing <a href="/wiki/Cartel" title="Cartel">cartel</a> for rice.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> This is seen by some as an action to capitalise on the crisis.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In June 2008 the <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Agriculture_Organization" title="Food and Agriculture Organization">Food and Agriculture Organization</a> hosted a <a href="/wiki/High-Level_Conference_on_World_Food_Security_(2008)" class="mw-redirect" title="High-Level Conference on World Food Security (2008)">High-Level Conference on World Food Security</a>, in which $1.2 billion in food aid was committed for the 75 million people in 60 countries hardest hit by rising food prices.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup></p>
<p>In June 2008, a sustained commitment from the <a href="/wiki/G8" class="mw-redirect" title="G8">G8</a> was called for by some humanitarian organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Food_price_decreases">Food price decreases</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007%E2%80%9308_world_food_price_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Food price decreases">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In December 2008, the <a href="/wiki/Late-2000s_recession" class="mw-redirect" title="Late-2000s recession">global economic slowdown</a>, <a href="/wiki/2000s_energy_crisis#Falling_prices_in_late_2008" title="2000s energy crisis">decreasing oil prices</a>, and speculation of decreased demand for commodities worldwide brought about sharp decreases in the price of staple crops from their earlier highs. Corn prices on the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Board_of_Trade" title="Chicago Board of Trade">Chicago Board of Trade</a> dropped from US$7.99 per bushel in June to US$3.74 per bushel in mid-December; wheat and rice prices experienced similar decreases.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> The UN's Food and Agriculture Organization, however, warned against "a false sense of security", noting that the <a href="/wiki/Subprime_mortgage_crisis" title="Subprime mortgage crisis">credit crisis</a> could cause farmers to reduce plantings.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> FAO convened a <a href="/wiki/World_Summit_on_Food_Security" class="mw-redirect" title="World Summit on Food Security">World Summit on Food Security</a> at its headquarters in Rome in November 2008, noting that food prices remained high in developing countries and that the global <a href="/wiki/Food_security" title="Food security">food security</a> situation has worsened.</p>
<p>By early 2011 food prices had risen again to surpass the record highs of 2008. Some commentators saw this as the resumption of the price spike seen in 2007–08.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> Prices had dropped after good weather helped increase grain yields while demand had dropped due to the recession.<sup id="cite_ref-Brown_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brown-161">[161]</a></sup></p>
